# portfolio
Harold's public portfolio for Telling Stories with Data Class

# About me
I trained as an engineer but my professional experience has been in consulting and product management. I am currently in the MISM-BIDA program. My interests lie in the intersection betweeen business and technology

# What I hope to learn
* In my professional life I frequently found it challenging to communicate new insights or findings in a visual medium. 
The first part of the challenge was in figuring out how best to lay out my ideas. 
Secondly, my audience was typically not familiar with non-bar chart visuals which limited my options. 
* Therefore, my goal is to refine how I communicate complex ideas in a visual medium. I would like to be communicate data insights/predictions/analysis more simply, clearly, and convincingly.

# Portfolio
My portfolio will be organized in the section below

### Rationale for Selecting Area Graph

There were two main insights looking at the data (and the earlier plots). Among the OECD countries, there is a spectrum of GDP-to-debt ratios. Also, these ratios have been changing over time (observable increase since 2008 for most countries). I wanted to tell both stories in one chart which is why I selected an area graph.

Countries with the highest ratios are sorted to the top of the chart. Additionally, this chart type has the advantage of horizontal axes for each country which makes trends (changes in GDP ratio over time) more observable

An interesting visualization be a scatter plot of a country's GDP on one axis and Debt on another axis. It would communicate GDP-to-debt ratio and also relative size of economies which is lost in these visualization. However, the raw data to produce that visualization was not available

The following modifications were made:
  * Used proper country names instead of abbreviations
  * Country labels increased to 14pt bold font 
  * 2017 data was missing for some countries hence excluded for all countries
  * Corrected horizontal axes labels as we did previously and also set padding to zero. Additional padding only increased chart area (and whitespace) while lack of padding made chart more readable

Reviewing the Infogram Data Visualization Checklist, the following modifications were identified but could not be made due to RAW's limitations:
  * 2016 label cropped
  * Country labels would have been outside the chart area to make it more readable
  * Tick marks on vertical axes for cross-country comparisons

#### Color scheme
RAW automatically assigned diverging color scheme. Given that countries are best thought of as categorical data, I opted for a categorical/qualitative scheme. I selected a qualitative color scheme from ColorBrewer2.0 for 9 data classes and exported hex codes. I re-ordered the order of colors based on a color scheme inspired by documentation from the Vega website. I copied hex codes from ColorBrewer2.0 to RAW. As there were 36 countries, each color was used 4 times. The pattern was applied to sorted list of colors so the effect of reader easily distinguishing  between countries was achieved

http://colorbrewer2.org/#type=qualitative&scheme=Paired&n=9

https://vega.github.io/vega/docs/schemes/


### Comparison of visualization methods

**Bar Chart**

Pros | Cons
--- | ---
Can interpolate values visually | Does not provide historical trends 
Simple | 
Readable | 

**Beeswarm plot**

Pros | Cons
--- | ---
Bubble size = values | Diminished readability due to scrolling to see all the data
Good for time series | Alphabetical ordering does not aid storytelling
 | Hard to compare bubble sizes across countries
 | Macro story hard (all OECD) is hard to tell
 
 **Area Graph**

Pros | Cons
--- | ---
Countries can be compared both historically and currently | Relative scale. Exact values cannot be read off chart
Individual time series for each country | Alphabetical ordering does not aid storytelling
